45:"$Sreact.suspense"
4:T8a8,1) 总体架构：120.6B总参、每token激活12.7B（不含embedding为12.1B）的MoE；骨干为周期性交织的Hybrid Mamba-Attention（继承Nemotron-3 Nano思路），在吞吐上利用Mamba类线性时间模块，在关键层保留Attention以维持建模能力。

2) LatentMoE（核心创新之一）：从硬件-软件共设计出发重新审视MoE。
- 论文明确区分两种瓶颈：
  a) 低延迟在线推理：主要受“读取专家权重”的内存带宽限制（专家矩阵大小 d×m）；
  b) 吞吐导向分布式推理：主要受all-to-all路由通信限制（路由体积 d×K）。
- 关键设计原则：在不牺牲质量的前提下，保持有效非线性预算 K·m 不变，同时尽量降低d（hidden dim）以缓解带宽与通信；但d不能无限降，受任务有效特征秩 r_eff 下界约束。
- LatentMoE据此在结构上做了不同于“传统FFN专家堆叠”的改造（报告中称其同时提升accuracy/parameter与accuracy/FLOP），目标是把“稀疏带来的理论省算”落到“实际省带宽、省通信、省显存”的可部署效率上。

3) MTP（Multi-Token Prediction）：在预训练中加入多token预测层，使模型天然支持speculative decoding（原生推测解码）以加速生成；同时作者声称MTP还能提升整体模型质量（通常来自更强的训练信号/更好的表示学习）。

4) 低精度预训练：首次在Nemotron 3家族中使用NVFP4完成预训练，强调稳定性与精度保持；并提供NVFP4/FP8/BF16等形态的开源权重。

5) 数据与训练阶段：25T tokens两阶段配比：
- Phase 1：20T（80%）强调多样性与覆盖；
- Phase 2：5T（20%）强调高质量与benchmark对齐。
这是一种典型的“先广覆盖后高质量收敛”的数据scaling策略。

6) 长上下文：最终模型支持最高1M context（报告称final model supports up to 1M context length），属于长上下文扩展的工程化落地。

7) 后训练：SFT + RL，且显著扩大agentic RL环境与数据，采用大规模异步RL基础设施提升鲁棒性；并开源GenRM（Qwen3-Nemotron-235B-A22B-GenRM-2603）与面向代码/逻辑/经济学/选择题等的合成数据集。5:T613,Architecture and training stack:
1) Model: 120.6B total parameters with 12.7B active per token (12.1B excluding embeddings). Backbone is a periodic interleaving of Mamba-style sequence modules and attention layers, aiming to improve throughput while preserving modeling capacity.
2) LatentMoE: derived from a hardware–software co-design analysis.
- For low-latency serving, MoE is often memory-bandwidth bound by reading expert weights (expert matrix size d×m).
- For throughput-oriented distributed serving, MoE is often communication bound by all-to-all routing (routing volume d×K).
- To preserve quality, keep the effective nonlinearity budget K·m; reduce d where possible, but d is lower-bounded by an effective feature rank r_eff.
LatentMoE implements a structural variant of MoE intended to improve both accuracy/FLOP and accuracy/parameter in practice (not just on paper).
3) MTP (Multi-Token Prediction): adds multi-token prediction layers during pretraining to enable “native” speculative decoding and reportedly improve model quality.
4) Pretraining precision: NVFP4 end-to-end pretraining (first in Nemotron 3 family), with released checkpoints in NVFP4/FP8/BF16.
5) Data scaling: 25T tokens in two phases—20T (diversity/coverage) then 5T (higher-quality, benchmark-focused).
6) Long context: final model supports up to 1M context.
7) Post-training: SFT + RL with expanded agentic environments and large-scale asynchronous RL infrastructure; releases a GenRM and multiple synthetic datasets targeting code/algorithms/logic/econ/MCQ.6:T40f,Deep-read priorities:
1) LatentMoE section (§2.1.1): focus on the bandwidth/communication cost model, the derived design rules (keep K·m, reduce d subject to r_eff), and the concrete architectural differences vs common MoEs (routing, expert shapes, sharding implications).
2) MTP section (§2.1.2): how multi-token prediction is implemented (loss, heads, horizon), how it improves quality, and how it enables native speculative decoding.
3) Data staging (20T+5T): composition, filtering, and what “benchmark-focused” means in practice—high value for data scaling decisions.
4) NVFP4 training details: stability mechanisms, optimizer/scaling, and any reported accuracy gaps.
5) Long-context to 1M: positional/attention changes and training curriculum.
6) RL infrastructure: if you care about RL-pretrain/agentic scaling, examine the asynchronous RL design and environment breadth.

Core novelty is concentrated in: deployability-driven MoE design (LatentMoE) + training–inference co-design via MTP + large-scale NVFP4 pretraining.7:T679,1) Dynamical-systems reframing: middle-looped transformers are written as a nonlinear time-varying dynamical system over the residual stream, with matrices controlling state carryover (\overline{A}), input injection (\overline{B}), and a nonlinear operator (\overline{R}) subsuming attention/MLP modules.

2) Linearized stability analysis: by linearizing (dropping \overline{R}), the update becomes an LTI system, enabling classic control-theory reasoning: divergence/residual explosion occurs when the effective state-update has too large a spectral norm. The authors argue prior looped recipes can learn such unstable \overline{A}-like injection parameterizations, empirically correlating with training blow-ups and loss spikes.

3) Parcae architecture: they introduce an explicit continuous-time representation A, discretize it, and parameterize A as a negative diagonal matrix. This constrains the spectrum to be contractive, preventing residual explosion by construction.

4) Training stabilizers for loss spikes: (i) an additional normalization on the input representation e to mitigate late-stage spikes, and (ii) a modified stochastic-depth objective implementation via intra-batch per-sequence depth sampling, reducing spike frequency/variance when optimizing expected loss over variable loop counts.

5) Scaling-law modeling: under parameter-matched isoFLOP comparisons, they fit FLOP-optimal power laws showing data and looping should co-increase; at test time, increasing recurrence yields predictable exponential decay toward an irreducible loss, and they combine train-time and test-time laws into a unified scaling relation for looped models.8:T532,LoSA is built on an empirical property of block-wise denoising: between consecutive denoising steps, only a small subset of tokens undergo large hidden-state/query changes (Active tokens), while most tokens remain nearly unchanged (Stable tokens). The method:
- Splits attention into prefix (cached Kp,Vp) and suffix (current block Kb,Vb) components and relies on an online-softmax/FlashAttention-style decomposition so partial outputs and normalizers can be cached and merged correctly.
- At step t, computes sparse prefix attention only for Active tokens (compatible with existing sparse selectors such as QUEST-like schemes), while reusing cached prefix-attention outputs for Stable tokens from step t-1.
- By reducing the number of queries participating in sparse prefix attention from B to |A|, it shrinks the union of accessed KV indices/pages, directly mitigating KV Inflation and lowering memory traffic.
- Quality improves relative to naive sparse attention because Stable tokens effectively keep a higher-fidelity prefix-attention signal (reused from a prior computation) instead of being forced through an aggressively sparse read every step.
Active/Stable detection is driven by inter-step query/representation change metrics (e.g., MSE or norm deltas) with a thresholding policy described in the main method sections.9:T579,KoCo (Knowledge Coordinate Conditioning) assigns each document a 3D discrete coordinate T=(s,c,t): Source (channel/carrier, e.g., academic vs social), Content (functional form/style, e.g., tutorial/reference/log), and Stability (expected temporal validity inferred from update frequency, e.g., evergreen vs ephemeral).
- Tagging: a lightweight LLM (Qwen-3-4B in the paper) predicts the three labels from URL + document text; the authors claim >99.5% coverage on DCLM.
- Conditioning: the labels are serialized into a natural-language prefix ("Source: ...; Content: ...; Stability: ...") prepended to the document. Training computes loss only on the original document tokens, treating the prefix as a conditioning variable rather than a target.
- Positioning vs prior work: unlike URL prefixes, the coordinate is coarser but intended to be more objective and less sparse; unlike data selection, it keeps noisy data but contextualizes it, aiming to mimic how humans discount rather than erase low-quality information.
- Inference-time control: the model can be prompted/conditioned with “more reliable” coordinates to reduce hallucinations (evaluated on TruthfulQA per the paper).
Conceptually, this is discrete metadata-to-text-prefix conditional LM; the real novelty is the coordinate design (topic-agnostic yet predictive of reliability/utility) and whether the gains persist under noisy tagging.a:T4db,Latent-Condensed Attention (LCA) performs context condensation natively in MLA’s latent space.
- MLA recap: cache semantic latents C^{KV} and positional keys K^R (RoPE), reconstruct per-head Q/K/V via up-projections; memory is reduced but attention remains dense over length L.
- LCA idea: condense tokens into fewer representatives, but treat semantic and positional components differently:
  1) Semantic condensation: partition the context into groups and aggregate the semantic latents within each group using query-aware weighted pooling, producing a compact set of semantic representatives.
  2) Positional preservation: instead of averaging positional keys, select a hard anchor token per group (the most relevant to the current query) and use its K^R to represent the group’s position, avoiding RoPE mixing and preserving relative-position fidelity.
- Properties: no additional parameters; can be integrated into pretrained models with lightweight finetuning; the paper claims a uniform approximation error bound independent of context length. The decoupled strategy is also claimed to generalize beyond MLA (e.g., to GQA).
Practically, LCA resembles latent-space token pooling/eviction with a RoPE-safe positional anchor mechanism.b:T457,Paradigms:
- PA: predict the judge score for the would-be response, then answer/act (or route).
- RPRA: add a reasoning step before prediction and another before answering, aiming to improve both score prediction and final output.

Implementation regimes: zero-shot, in-context learning, and supervised fine-tuning.

Calibration fixes:
1) Report card (training-free): build a textual performance summary from a model’s historical judge-evaluated results across multiple datasets, using modal judge ratings to describe typical strengths/weaknesses; prepend this to prompts so the model can condition its self-score prediction on known performance.
2) Fine-tuning for prediction (report-card-free at inference): use the hindsight trick to relabel examples with judge scores after observing responses, then SFT models to directly predict the judge score from the prompt, enabling PA without extra report-card tokens.

Model suite: broad range from ~0.9B to 120B/70B-class models (MobileLLM, Llama 3.x variants, GPT OSS, DeepSeek distilled Qwen variants, Llama 4 Scout) to compare size effects on self-evaluation.c:T446,CLASP has two coupled modules, both conditioned on instruction category. (1) Class-adaptive layer fusion: instead of extracting visual tokens from a single ViT layer, it fuses multi-layer ViT features with category-dependent weights, aiming to retain the right granularity (shallower/mid layers for local-detail tasks like counting; deeper layers for semantic tasks). The paper motivates this with a category-wise sensitivity study (Fig. 1 top). (2) Class-adaptive dual-stage pruning: token reduction is split into two stages with an explicit token-budget allocation. Stage-1 is relevance-preserving, keeping attention-salient pivot/evidence tokens. Stage-2 is coverage-oriented, using redundancy-aware/similarity criteria to keep complementary context while further removing redundant patches. The balance between attention-led and similarity-led pruning is also category-adaptive (motivated by Fig. 1 bottom showing different optimal mixing ratios per category). The method is positioned as plug-and-play before the projector/LLM, reducing the number of visual tokens consumed by the decoder.d:T500,Vector Relieved Flash Attention (VFA) modifies the online-softmax update schedule to avoid repeated rowmax-driven updates and the associated rescale chain:
1) mm-initialization: before streaming all key blocks, initialize the per-row running maximum with a cheap approximation computed from dot-products between each query row and precomputed key-block representations. The paper argues naive Q/K block summaries fail due to intra-block heterogeneity (directional similarity not high enough; large norm variance).
2) Key-block traversal reordering: process a sink block and the query-aligned local block(s) first, motivated by empirical evidence that attention mass and the eventual running-max often stabilize early in these regions.
3) Max-freezing: after the prioritized blocks, freeze the running maximum for the remaining blocks—skip per-block rowmax reductions and the rescale chain—while still accumulating exp(S - m) and PV using the same online-softmax state variables.
4) Composition with BLASST: combining VFA with online block skipping yields VSA, pairing fewer processed blocks with cheaper per-block statistic overhead. The paper highlights that VFA/VSA bypass the rescale operation in the update stage, avoiding conditional branching used in FA4.0-like designs.e:T40e,Built on top of vLLM, the design centers on making KV cache resizable and migratable while keeping source and target PP configurations coexisting safely:
- A coordination protocol orchestrates weight loading, layer remapping, KV migration, and the final cutover while continuing to serve requests.
- KV resizing challenge: existing PageAttention-style systems often preallocate each layer’s KV as a contiguous region, which cannot be resized in place; naive block-level allocation is inefficient due to coarse GPU allocation granularity and internal fragmentation.
- Non-contiguous KV block access extends PageAttention to allow KV to be managed as blocks that can grow/shrink.
- Layer stacking packs multiple layers’ KV states into a single allocation unit to better match GPU allocation granularity and reduce fragmentation.
- KV patching (inspired by VM live migration) incrementally migrates KV during inference to keep divergence small, then reconciles the residual with a short final pause instead of a long stop-and-copy stall.f:T5f0,The contribution is a dynamic curation pipeline plus a four-scenario evaluation protocol.
1) Dynamic parametric filtering: collect heterogeneous KB-VQA samples S0 with x=(q,v,K,a). Query a set of strong open(-ish) VLMs as gating models (Gemma3-27B, Qwen-2.5-VL-32B, InternVL3-38B, VL-Rethinker-72B) in a parametric setting (q,v only, no external knowledge). Use an external judge (GPT-4o with a SimpleQA-style prompt) to label each response as CORRECT / INCORRECT / NOT ATTEMPTED, mapped to Accuracy / Hallucination / Deflection. Keep only items that all gating models fail, yielding S1 intended to be genuinely retrieval-dependent.
2) Context augmentation: for each retained item, attach gold context K(x)^+ and distractor context K(x)^-. If negatives are not provided by the source, mine them via retrieval: build a Wikipedia text index, retrieve with EVA-CLIP, segment passages, and rerank with Contriever; for visual negatives, retrieve top-10 similar non-gold images from an image index.
3) Quality control: enforce solvability with gold context and difficulty/robustness under distractors (details/thresholds appear later in the full paper).
4) Evaluation protocol: define four complementary settings—parametric, oracle (gold context), realistic (retrieved mixed context), adversarial (distracting/contradictory context)—to separate memorization, upper-bound grounding, real-world RAG robustness, and adversarial susceptibility, while explicitly tracking hallucination vs deflection rather than accuracy alone.10:T4b5,TIPSv2 builds on TIPS with a joint loss L = L_CLIP + L_DINO + L_iBOT, and introduces several changes:
- Patch-level distillation study: applying teacher supervision to all patch tokens yields large gains in patch-text alignment, with the student exceeding the teacher. The paper attributes this to two implementation drivers: removing masking that makes token supervision sparse, and initialization choices that steer optimization toward locally semantic representations.
- iBOT++: a new masked self-supervised objective designed to internalize the distillation benefit by enforcing representation consistency on visible tokens (dense constraints on patch embeddings), rather than relying on external teachers.
- Multi-granularity text augmentation: combines web alt-text with synthetic captions (PaliGemma/Gemini) emphasizing spatial relations; uses separate global CLS embeddings aligned to different caption styles to better cover object-centric vs spatial semantics.
- Head-only EMA: instead of full-model EMA (common in DINO/iBOT), only the projection heads are EMA-updated, leveraging text supervision as a stabilizing anchor to reduce memory/training cost while retaining teacher-student stability.11:T468,The work combines diagnosis + a training-free fix.
Diagnosis: the authors compare visual attention maps between prefill and multiple decoding steps. VQA shows relatively stable focus, while visual reasoning exhibits frequent attention jumps to different image regions. They define this as RVIS and empirically link higher RVIS frequency to larger performance drops under pruning.
Method (DSTP: Decoding-stage Shift-aware Token Pruning): a plug-in wrapper over existing pruners (e.g., FastV, DivPrune). It keeps the pruned-away tokens in a cache for potential recovery, and during decoding performs:
- RISD (shift detection): monitors decoding-time visual attention and triggers when attention distribution indicates a shift in relevant regions (threshold-based).
- CPTS (Context-Preserving Token Swap): when RVIS is detected, it swaps currently kept visual tokens with newly relevant ones retrieved from the discarded pool, aiming to restore missing evidence while keeping the context stable.
No retraining, no parameter updates; the goal is to preserve most pruning efficiency while preventing reasoning-step evidence mismatch.12:T50c,DocSeeker is built on Qwen-2.5-VL-7B-Instruct without adding extra modules; the novelty is in the reasoning paradigm and training recipe:
1) ALR (Analysis–Localization–Reasoning) paradigm: treat each page as an image; prefix each page’s visual tokens with a page-id pointer. The model outputs a structured trace: analyze intent → localize evidence with explicit page ids → reason from that evidence → produce the final answer plus cited page ids.
2) Two-stage training:
- Stage I SFT: generate high-quality ALR chain-of-thought annotations via an efficient distillation pipeline from a strong teacher, then supervise the model to internalize the ALR workflow.
- Stage II EviGRPO: Evidence-aware Group Relative Policy Optimization that jointly optimizes evidence localization and reasoning/answering.
3) EGRA (Evidence-Guided Resolution Allocation): a training-time strategy used in both stages to allocate resolution/compute more effectively for long visual sequences, reducing memory pressure while strengthening supervision (presumably by prioritizing evidence-relevant pages/regions).
Unlike system-level visual RAG that retrieves top-k pages externally, DocSeeker trains evidence localization as an intrinsic model capability and makes grounding explicit via page-id pointers.13:T47d,SpotSound builds on strong ALM backbones (Qwen2-Audio, Audio Flamingo 3) with Whisper-large-v3 as the audio encoder. The method has three pillars:
1) Two-stage formulation: first predict event existence (yes/no) for a query; only if yes, generate all matching (start,end) intervals. This gating isolates verification from localization.
2) Timestamp-interleaved encoding: inject temporal information by interleaving discrete timestamp tokens with audio embeddings, turning continuous time into a token sequence the LLM can attend to and generate against. With the encoder’s temporal compression, each audio timestep corresponds to ~40 ms.
3) Hallucination-suppressing objective via discriminative quadruplets: each instance is restructured as (audio, positive query, ground-truth timestamps, negative query for an absent event). Training enforces correct localization for positives while teaching the model to reject negatives (no timestamps), directly penalizing “timestamp hallucinations.” The authors also assemble a temporally-aware instruction-tuning set totaling 77.6k samples (10k newly curated + 67.6k collected from existing datasets).14:T54f,Analysis: aggregate decoder attention mass over video frames during generation; define the frame with the maximum aggregated frame-level attention as the anchor frame. The authors report a stable, temporally imbalanced concentration pattern that is largely independent of the input video (content-agnostic, model-specific). They further observe that broad temporal evidence becomes increasingly under-used in mid-to-late decoder layers, where anchor dominance strengthens and correlates with temporal reasoning failures.

Method (DTR, Decoder-side Temporal Rebalancing): a simple, training-free, layer-selective intervention applied to the decoder’s temporal attention in selected mid-to-late layers. DTR suppresses over-concentration on the anchor frame and compensates under-attended frames in a broad/adaptive manner, aiming to rebalance temporal evidence flow into later layers and token prediction. It is positioned as a plug-in: no retraining, no video re-sampling or prompt tricks, no auxiliary models, and no multi-branch decoding.

Difference from prior work: many video hallucination mitigations rely on training (alignment/preference optimization) or inference-time complexity (input modification, auxiliary guidance, contrastive decoding). DTR directly targets the temporal evidence allocation mechanism inside the decoder with minimal overhead.15:T41b,From the provided full-text excerpt, the experimentally supported claims we can safely extract are mostly qualitative/mechanistic:
- strong temporal attention imbalance with a definable anchor frame;
- the concentration pattern is reported to be largely input-independent (content-agnostic bias);
- case studies show anchor over-focus leads to missing key action phases and wrong temporal judgments, consistent with hallucinations;
- the paper claims further analyses/experiments confirm correlation with hallucination and that DTR mitigates it.

However, the supplied content is truncated before the full method specification and the experimental section (benchmarks, metrics, model sizes, layer choices, ablations, and numeric gains are missing). Without those sections, I cannot responsibly report quantitative improvements or detailed ablation findings “based on the full paper”. If you provide the remaining sections/PDF, I can extract the exact tables (hallucination rate drops, benchmark deltas, layer/strength ablations, runtime overhead).16:T403,Skim plan (20–30 minutes; longer if you add the missing experiment section):
1) Intro + Fig. 1: understand the anchor-frame definition and the content-agnostic bias hypothesis.
2) DTR method: focus on (a) which layers are intervened, (b) the exact reweighting rule on temporal attention, (c) whether it is head-wise or aggregated, and (d) any safeguards to avoid over-smoothing.
3) Experiments/analysis (once available): prioritize (i) anchor stability across videos/prompts/tasks, (ii) correlation between attention concentration metrics (entropy/Gini) and hallucination, (iii) layer ablations showing why mid-to-late layers matter.

Deep-dive angle for pretraining researchers: translate DTR into training-time regularizers/objectives for temporal coverage and study whether such constraints improve scaling behavior and reduce hallucination without inference-time hacks.17:T4ee,The paper’s contribution is a mechanism-driven taxonomy and causal analysis:
1) Definition/scope: hallucination = fluent but contradicting observable spatiotemporal evidence; emphasizes why image-hallucination taxonomies do not transfer due to causality/temporal grounding/motion dynamics/audio-visual integration.
2) Taxonomy by observable failure modes (not by input attributes):
- Dynamic Distortion: entities may be detected, but their temporal progression or referential consistency is wrong. Subtypes: (i) spatiotemporal dynamics errors (event order, duration, frequency/counting), (ii) referential inconsistency (identity/scene conflation across time).
- Content Fabrication: outputs driven by priors or audio rather than visual evidence. Subtypes: (i) context-driven completions from co-occurrence priors, (ii) audio-visual conflict where audio overrides vision.
3) Root-cause mapping: distortion ↔ missing fine-grained motion cues, weak long-range memory, poor temporal localization; fabrication ↔ insufficient visual grounding enabling pretrained priors or dominant audio signals.
4) Research directions: motion-aware architectures to preserve temporal features; counterfactual training to disentangle evidence from priors and reduce fabrication.18:T507,1) Sparse MoE Diffusion Transformer: 64 routed experts per layer, ~17B total parameters, but only ~2B activated per forward pass.
2) Routing: Expert-Choice Routing (experts select tokens) to keep utilization balanced with less reliance on heavy auxiliary load-balancing losses.
3) Conditioning redesign: exclude text tokens from the main Transformer backbone; use a joint-attention mechanism so text-side KV can be shared across diffusion timesteps, cutting repeated computation and memory.
4) Decoupled routing for stability: timestep modulation can shift feature distributions and destabilize routing; the paper introduces a decoupled routing design that separates routing signals from timestep-modulated activations to improve training stability and expert assignment consistency.
5) Training objective & curriculum: rectified flow supervision plus a multi-stage curriculum that increases the emphasis on higher-quality data tiers later in training.
6) Data pipeline: ~700M curated images and ~1.5B image-caption pairs; a metadata-first design (Parquet control plane + immutable snapshots/manifests) enabling fast iteration, debuggability, and deterministic sampling via attached signals (quality tiers, curriculum buckets K=8, aspect-ratio buckets, caption provenance, routing tags).19:T406,VideoFlexTok is an autoencoder-style tokenizer with (i) a 2D token organization (time × coarse-to-fine level), (ii) training that induces a prefix-to-detail hierarchy, and (iii) a generative decoder that can decode from any token count. Concretely: it operates in a video VAE latent space for efficiency; uses learnable register tokens per time step and interleaves latent frames and registers in the input sequence. A coarse-to-fine hierarchy along the register dimension is induced via nested dropout that randomly drops a suffix of register tokens, forcing good reconstructions from short prefixes. Because pure reconstruction tends to encode pixel-level detail early, it adds a semantic bias by distilling features from a pretrained self-supervised vision encoder (DINOv2), encouraging early tokens to carry semantic/geometric/motion information. The decoder is trained as a generative rectified flow model, enabling plausible, realistic video generation conditioned on any number of tokens—more tokens yield finer details.1a:Taba,全文结构是“现象学→机制→配方→成本/局限”的闭环。

(1) 现象学：两条成功条件
- 条件 A：Thinking-pattern consistency（思维模式一致）。作者用 student 与 teacher 的 top-k token 分布重叠度（overlap ratio）来刻画：如果初始重叠很低，即便 teacher benchmark 更高，OPD 也可能无法把 student 拉到 teacher 分布附近。
- 条件 B：Higher scores ≠ 新知识。即使思维模式一致、teacher 分数更高，如果 teacher 与 student 来自同数据同训练配方、只是 scale 更大，那么从 student 视角看 teacher 分布可能“不可区分”（distributionally indistinguishable），teacher 并没有提供 student 未见过的可迁移信号，OPD 增益会很小。
- 通过 weak-to-strong 的 reverse distillation 进一步验证：OPD 学到的本质是“思维模式/分布形状”，而不是简单地追逐 benchmark 分数。

(2) token 级机制：梯度信号的主承载体是 overlap tokens
- 成功 OPD 的统一签名：在 student 访问到的状态上，student 与 teacher 分布逐步变得更相似：top-k overlap ratio 持续上升；两者 entropy gap 逐渐缩小；重叠 token 集合承载了 97–99% 的联合概率质量。
- 失败 OPD：overlap 停滞、entropy mismatch 从一开始就存在并持续。
- 关键验证：只对“重叠 token 集合”施加监督，效果可匹配完整 top-k 监督，说明 OPD 的有效梯度主要来自重叠集；非重叠部分对优化贡献小或噪声大。

(3) Recipe：两种互补的失败修复策略
- Off-policy cold start：先用 teacher 生成的 rollouts 做一段 SFT warmup，提高初始 overlap，缩小思维模式差距，再切换到 OPD。
- Teacher-aligned prompt selection：用 teacher 后训练数据分布中的 prompts 来做 OPD，使监督集中在 teacher 高概率 token 上，更易对齐；但会导致 student entropy 显著降低（更“尖”/更保守），因此需要与 out-of-distribution prompts 混合以避免过拟合/塌缩。

(4) 稠密监督的成本与长轨迹问题
- reward 质量随 trajectory depth 系统性下降；不稳定性往往从后段 token 开始并向前传播。
- 重要观察：即便“失败 teacher”，其 reward 与 rollout 正确性在全局上仍相关，失败更像是局部优化几何问题：更大的 teacher 可能让 student 附近的 reward landscape 局部变平，导致 token 级梯度虽“方向正确”但幅度/曲率不足以推动策略更新。

整体上，作者把 OPD 从经验技巧提升为可诊断、可修复、可解释的训练算子，并给出一套与 token 分布几何直接对应的指标体系（overlap、entropy gap、probability mass concentration）。1b:T444,For foundation-model training research, the contribution is a rare mechanism-driven account of a widely used post-training primitive:
- It replaces the naive "stronger teacher helps" assumption with two testable distributional requirements (thinking-pattern compatibility and genuine novelty beyond the student’s training exposure), which is directly relevant to scaling, continual distillation, and data/recipe design.
- It identifies a concrete locus of effective gradients: the student–teacher top-k overlap tokens, supported by dynamics (overlap growth, entropy-gap closure, probability-mass concentration). This can inform more stable OPD objectives and diagnostics.
- It provides actionable recovery recipes (off-policy cold start; teacher-aligned prompt selection) and analyzes dense-supervision degradation with trajectory depth—highly relevant for long-horizon reasoning and agentic rollouts.

While not a new pretraining objective, it elevates OPD into a measurable, debuggable operator for continual improvement pipelines and potentially RL-pretrain-style self-bootstrapping.1c:T7ac,The paper is organized as phenomenology → mechanism → recipe → cost/limits.

1) Phenomenology: two governing conditions.
(A) Thinking-pattern consistency: student and teacher must have compatible next-token distributions, quantified via top-k overlap ratio. If initial overlap is low, OPD often cannot recover even if the teacher scores higher.
(B) Higher benchmark scores do not imply new transferable knowledge: if teacher and student share the same data and training recipe (only scale differs), they may converge to distributions that are indistinguishable from the student’s perspective, leaving little signal for OPD.
Reverse distillation experiments are used to validate these claims and to argue OPD primarily learns "thinking patterns" (distributional behavior) rather than merely chasing benchmark metrics.

2) Token-level mechanism.
Successful OPD shows a consistent signature on student-visited states: increasing top-k overlap, shrinking entropy gap, and the overlap set capturing nearly all probability mass. Failing runs show stagnant overlap and persistent entropy mismatch.
A key test: supervising only the overlap tokens matches full top-k supervision, implying the overlap set is the main carrier of useful gradients.

3) Practical recipes.
- Off-policy cold start: warm up with SFT on teacher-generated rollouts to raise initial overlap, then switch to OPD.
- Teacher-aligned prompt selection: use prompts from the teacher’s post-training distribution to sharpen alignment on high-probability tokens; mitigate entropy collapse by mixing with out-of-distribution prompts.

4) Cost/instability with depth.
Reward quality degrades with trajectory depth; instability starts at later tokens and propagates backward. Even "failing" teachers provide globally informative reward, suggesting failure is due to local optimization geometry (e.g., a locally flat landscape around the student induced by a larger teacher), not purely reward noise.1d:T43b,Deep-read guide (2–3 hours, aiming to reuse the recipe):
- Section 3 (Phenomenology): focus on how thinking-pattern consistency is measured (top-k overlap definition, choice of k, thresholds) and how "new knowledge" is operationalized in reverse distillation.
- Section 4 (Mechanism): study the plots for overlap ratio, entropy gap, and probability-mass concentration; the overlap-only supervision experiment is the key mechanistic evidence.
- Section 5 (Recipe): treat as an implementation manual—how long the cold start is, how prompts are selected/mixed, and how entropy collapse is monitored.
- Section 6 (Cost/Instability): extract the depth-vs-reward degradation curves and the instability propagation analysis; this sets the boundary for long-horizon reasoning/agentic OPD.

Research angles worth probing: online overlap-based diagnostics/early stopping, objectives that explicitly increase overlap, verifying the "local flatness" hypothesis via curvature/gradient-noise analyses, and hybrid schemes for long trajectories (segmenting, reweighting, mixing outcome rewards).1e:T424,This is a high-impact post-training paper with clear implications for scalable foundation-model training:
- Conceptual contribution: elevates “teacher consistency” from an implementation detail to a necessary condition, explaining systematic failures when SFT demonstrations come from one model while OPD supervision comes from another. The claim is strong: inconsistency induces an irreducible bias and a suboptimal fixed point even for online OPD, not just offline.
- Practical contribution: Lightning OPD removes the need for parallel teacher serving by caching teacher log-probs offline, reporting ~4× speedup while matching or exceeding standard OPD on reasoning/code benchmarks.
- Broader research lesson relevant to continual learning / self-distillation / RL-pretrain-like pipelines: mixing a data-generation policy and a different token-level supervising policy can bake in objective bias that does not vanish with more compute or data, so “distributional alignment” between generation and supervision matters as much as raw teacher strength.1f:T5bf,1) Empirical motivation: student policies in OPD tend to drift only modestly from the SFT reference (consistent with observations that RL trajectories are largely reweighted SFT trajectories and KL constraints keep policies near the reference), suggesting offline reuse of teacher scores might work.
2) Root-cause analysis: OPD implicitly involves two teachers—an SFT teacher that produced the trajectories used to train the reference policy, and an OPD teacher that provides token-level distribution targets/advantages during distillation. If these differ, the OPD objective becomes biased; the paper argues this bias is irreducible and leads to convergence to a suboptimal fixed point regardless of training length or data scale. Offline OPD is further harmed because the rollout distribution is fixed to the (already mismatched) reference.
3) Lightning OPD (offline OPD done right): choose a single teacher π_T; (i) generate SFT trajectories with π_T and fine-tune the base model to obtain π_ref; (ii) sample rollouts from π_ref and precompute π_T log-probabilities once over these fixed responses; (iii) train the student with OPD using cached teacher scores—no live teacher server.
4) Theory claims: under teacher consistency, Lightning OPD shares the same optimum as standard OPD; the gradient discrepancy remains bounded during training; and the offline objective provides implicit regularization that limits policy drift without an explicit penalty term.20:T5c7,Two-stage framework:

1) Semantic Bottleneck identification.
- For each prompt with multiple language realizations, collect hidden states at each layer.
- Define two partitions of representations: grouped by language identity vs grouped by semantic equivalence (same query across languages).
- Compute Silhouette scores for both partitions per layer; the bottleneck layer is where semantic grouping dominates language grouping the most.
- Empirical signature: semantic Silhouette follows an inverted-U across depth; language Silhouette follows a U-shape; t-SNE shows early layers cluster by language, mid layers by meaning.

2) LASA (Language-Agnostic Semantic Alignment).
- Anchor safety alignment at the bottleneck layer rather than at the text level.
- Train a "Safety Semantic Interpreter" that reads bottleneck representations and extracts a safety-relevant semantic control signal.
- Condition generation on this semantic signal so that refusal/safe behavior depends on shared semantics, enabling cross-lingual generalization.

Conceptual difference vs prior multilingual safety: instead of adding low-resource safety data (SFT/DPO/RL) or transferring via reward shaping/self-distillation in text space, LASA attempts to bypass language distribution bias by aligning in a language-agnostic representational subspace.

Assumption/boundary: the base model must already exhibit strong cross-lingual semantic alignment (a clear bottleneck); otherwise the approach may not hold.21:T49f,PromptEcho reward: for a generated image x from prompt c, feed (x, a fixed guiding query q such as “Describe this image in detail.”) into a frozen VLM M, then treat the original prompt c as the label sequence and compute token-level cross-entropy over the positions of c. The reward is the negative CE:
- Deterministic: no autoregressive sampling of a description, avoiding randomness and VLM hallucinations in scoring.
- Fine-grained: token-level likelihood is intended to be sensitive to missing attributes, relations, and counting.
- Scalable: reward quality improves automatically with stronger open-source VLMs, without re-annotation or reward-model retraining.

RL optimization: they use Advantage Weighted Matching (AWM) for diffusion-model RL, emphasizing pure ODE sampling to avoid quality degradation from exploration noise. Pipeline: sample prompts → generate a group of images → compute PromptEcho rewards via frozen VLM → compute group-relative advantages → update the T2I model.

Data: an internal ~100K high-quality, concept-rich image set; Qwen3-VL-32B generates long (200–400 word) detailed captions under a fixed query to form the prompt distribution.22:T471,They analyze a layer output under fine-tuning by first-order Taylor expansion around a safe point (W0, h0), decomposing output drift into a term driven by activation change Δh and a term driven by weight change ΔW (dropping the second-order interaction ΔWΔh). This motivates the claim that:
- Weight-only constraints cannot prevent upstream representation reorganization (Δh) that bypasses safety pathways.
- Activation-only constraints leave the computation (ΔW) free to change and route around the constrained features.
CWAC couples two constraints:
1) Weight constraint: build a “safety subspace” / projection matrix from harmful-prompt statistics (covariance + SVD), and project/regularize updates so that perturbations do not change behavior on harmful prompts.
2) Activation constraint: train a sparse autoencoder on mixed benign/harmful data to identify safety-critical features, then add a targeted regularization term during fine-tuning to keep those feature activations close to the baseline model on held-out harmful prompts.
The combined objective applies both constraints during fine-tuning to close bypass routes.23:T5b9,KnowRL decomposes guidance into atomic Knowledge Points (KPs) and selects a compact, interaction-aware subset per problem:
1) Motivation/diagnosis: existing hinting implicitly treats guidance as a quantity expansion problem; empirically, performance vs hint ratio is highly non-linear (jump then diminishing returns), and longer hints can create branching ambiguity (cross-hint inconsistency).
2) KP decomposition: represent hints as a set of discrete KPs (the excerpt does not include the exact KP extraction/format details, but the framework assumes KPs are composable and prunable units).
3) Interaction awareness: introduce the pruning interaction paradox, suggesting KP dependencies/complimentarity; thus greedy pruning can be misleading.
4) Constrained Subset Search (CSS): a two-phase strategy—prune for leakage/redundancy first, then perform a global subset search over remaining candidates under constraints to find a minimal sufficient set that respects interactions.
5) Difficulty-aware injection during RL: easy instances get no hints; only hard instances receive the minimal KP subset, aiming to reduce reward sparsity with minimal token overhead.
Compared to fixed-ratio prefixes (QuestA/POPE), adaptive ratios (StepHint/UFT), or teacher-generated abstractions (TAPO/Guide/Scaf-GRPO), KnowRL’s key novelty is changing the optimization object from “hint length/ratio/template” to “discrete KP subset selection with interaction constraints.”24:T4b4,The approach has three main components:
1) Empirical training dynamics: during GRPO training, accuracy monotonically increases while AUC-mean monotonically worsens.
2) Theoretical diagnosis: the GRPO gradient is rewritten into a pairwise form using U-statistics, showing it is equivalent (in expectation) to optimizing pairwise differences (∇lpm(o1)−∇lpm(o2)) weighted by (R1−R2). The authors then argue/prove that this reward-difference-driven surrogate is inconsistent for calibration optimization, hence updates can systematically push probability mass toward fluent-but-wrong outputs, degrading relative calibration.
3) CAPO: a calibration-aware policy optimization method that replaces the uncertainty-agnostic advantage with an uncertainty-aware estimator derived from a consistent logistic AUC surrogate, enabling joint optimization of accuracy and calibration. A reference-model-based noise masking mechanism is added to stabilize training by suppressing noisy/unstable updates. The paper also provides gradient-based intuition: the learning dynamics prioritizes correcting samples whose confidence ranking contradicts correctness ranking (high-confidence wrong vs. low-confidence right).25:T46e,Shortcut Guardrail is a two-stage framework:
1) Shortcut token localization at test time: compute gradient-based saliency/attribution per input and treat top-attributed tokens as likely shortcut features. The paper claims these tokens align strongly with shortcut tokens in biased models (e.g., >90% recall in sentiment classification).
2) Unsupervised LoRA debiasing via Masked Contrastive Learning (MaskCL): train a lightweight LoRA adapter on unlabeled test batches. For each input, create augmented views by masking individual high-attribution tokens; optimize a contrastive/invariance objective that penalizes representation shift between the original and masked views. Intuition: if the model is overly dependent on a shortcut token, masking it causes large representation/prediction changes; enforcing invariance pushes the model to rely more on broader context/semantics.
A small labeled set is used only to calibrate the debiasing strength (Section 3.4), trading off robustness vs in-distribution retention.
They also propose MSTPS (Max Single-Token Prediction Sensitivity) to quantify reliance on single-token perturbations.26:T4bb,Built on the Joshi et al. (COLT 2025) PAC model:
- Base hypothesis class F consists of next-token generators f: Σ*→Σ.
- Iterating the apply-and-append operator T times yields a length-T trajectory (the “CoT”) and the final token (the e2e output). This induces derived classes F^{CoT,T} and F^{e2e,T}.
- Learning task: prompts x are drawn i.i.d. from an unknown distribution D; target generator f_*∈F. Training data reveals either (x, f_*^{e2e,T}(x)) or (x, f_*^{CoT,T}(x)), but evaluation is always end-to-end error on the final token.
- Core proof pattern: analyze how complexity blows up when learning the composed/iterated mapping under e2e-only labels (typically via lower-bound constructions where many distinct generators/trajectories alias to the same final outputs on observed samples), versus how full-trajectory supervision enables stepwise identification and yields substantially better (often polynomial-in-T) sample complexity upper bounds.
- The paper also discusses extensions beyond single “correct” outputs (multi-solution reasoning) via more general loss/multilabel viewpoints, which is crucial for mapping the theory to real CoT data where many intermediate chains can be valid.27:T932,方法上是“可控数据生成 + 最小可表达架构 + 机制归因/电路分析”的组合。
- 任务与数据：从对称 Dirichlet 分布一次性采样 K 个转移矩阵（固定不变），每个样本是一段长度≤N 的状态序列，训练目标是自回归预测下一个状态分布。K 是训练任务族多样性；因为 K 有限，模型既可能学到对每条链的参数记忆（识别链ID→读出转移），也可能学到对上下文统计的在线估计（对未见链也泛化）。
- 策略/阶段定义：
  * 1-Gen：只用 1-point（状态频率）做泛化预测；
  * 2-Gen：用 2-point（相邻转移计数）做泛化预测（对马尔可夫链是充分统计）；
  * 1-Mem：用 1-point 统计去“识别是哪条链”，再从参数中取出该链的转移；
  * 2-Mem：用 2-point 统计识别链并检索转移（更样本高效但更依赖参数存储）。
- 架构：两层 Transformer（每层 attention + MLP + residual stream + 最终线性读出），这是作者声称能覆盖四种策略的最小架构；固定 C=10, D=64。
- 机制刻画（论文主贡献）：作者声称给出“complete mechanistic characterization”，核心是把每个阶段对应到跨层的子回路（multi-layer subcircuits），并指出存在两类 qualitatively distinct 的上下文自适应机制（motifs）：
  1) 一类更像“统计估计器”：注意力在上下文中聚合计数/共现信息，把统计量写入 residual stream，后续模块将统计量映射为预测分布（对应 G1/G2）。
  2) 另一类更像“识别-检索器”：先在上下文中构造能区分链的指纹（1-point 或 2-point），再通过注意力/MLP 触发对参数中存储的特定链转移表的读出（对应 M1/M2）。
- 最小模型：作者还提到用 minimal models 隔离两种 motif 的关键特征，用于证明哪些结构要素是必要的（例如需要跨层协作、需要某种注意力检索通道等）。
（注：你提供的“全文内容”在 Paper 1 处被截断在 M2 介绍附近，后续用于支撑“complete mechanistic characterization”的具体电路、公式推导、可视化与定量归因细节未出现在当前文本中，因此这里对电路细节只能基于已给内容做结构化概括，无法逐图逐式复现作者的完整机制证明链条。）28:T6e1,The approach combines a controllable synthetic task family with a minimal transformer and mechanistic circuit analysis.
- Data/task: Sample K transition matrices once from a symmetric Dirichlet ensemble and keep them fixed; generate sequences from these stationary Markov chains; train autoregressively to predict the next discrete state. K controls training diversity.
- Algorithmic strategies/phases:
  * 1-Gen: generalize using only 1-point (state frequency) statistics;
  * 2-Gen: generalize using 2-point (adjacent transition) statistics (sufficient for Markov chains);
  * 1-Mem: use 1-point stats to identify which of the K chains is active, then retrieve its transitions from parameters;
  * 2-Mem: use 2-point stats for identification and retrieval (more sample-efficient but more parametric storage).
- Model: a 2-layer transformer (attention + MLP per layer with a residual stream and linear readout), claimed to be the simplest architecture that can realize all four strategies; C=10, D=64.
- Mechanistic claim: the four phases are implemented by multi-layer subcircuits exhibiting two distinct motifs for context-adaptive computation: (i) an “in-context estimator” motif that aggregates sufficient statistics into the residual stream and maps them to predictions (generalization phases), and (ii) an “identify-and-retrieve” motif that constructs a chain fingerprint from context and triggers parametric lookup of the corresponding transition table (memorization phases). Minimal models are used to isolate which architectural features are essential.
Note: the provided full-text excerpt is truncated before the detailed circuit evidence/derivations; thus, the description above is constrained to what is explicitly available in the excerpt.29:T957,核心是信息论/最小最大（minimax）分析，给出校准误差估计的下界并与可达上界匹配。
1）问题形式化：模型输出置信度 p(x)∈[0,1]，校准差 Δ(p)=η(p)−p，其中 η(p)=E[正确|p(X)=p]；考虑 Δ 属于 L-Lipschitz 函数类 F(L)。目标是用 m 个带标签样本估计 ECE（文中以 binned ECE 为例，但结论指向更广的校准误差估计）。
2）关键结论（被动/静态评测）：给出 minimax 风险 R*(m,ε,L)=inf_est sup_{Δ∈F(L)} E|Ĥ−H| 的最优速率为 Θ((L·ε/m)^{1/3})（忽略对数因子），并强调 ε 依赖是此前工作缺失的关键。直觉上：当错误稀有时，校准偏差也变成“稀有事件”，观测到足够多的错误以区分校准函数需要更高样本量；同时 Lipschitz 约束把“局部偏差”扩散到可检测尺度，形成 1/3 指数的非参数估计难度。
3）下界证明：构造两个分布/先验（P0 校准、P1 在 p0=1−ε 附近引入幅度 δ 的失配）使得 ECE 差异可控但 KL 散度也可控；通过 Bretagnolle–Huber 或两先验方法（Lepski et al.）把“不可区分性”转成风险下界。文中还给出在 score-mass 集中于 1−ε 附近时更强的 (Lε/m)^{1/3} 下界，并强调不依赖白噪声渐近等价（附录给出 Brown–Low 等价的替代推导）。
4）上界与可达性：用直方图/分箱估计并选择最优 bin 数 B*≈(L^2 m/ε)^{1/3} 达到同阶速率，完成 minimax 匹配。
5）四个“反直觉”结果：
- 自评无信息：任何不使用真实标签的估计（包括 LLM-as-judge、self-consistency、CoT verification、模型内部信号等）在最坏情形下对校准误差的估计无改进，甚至给出常数级下界（文中表述为 worst-case calibration error ≥1/2），除非白盒访问能把问题约束到低维参数族。
- 相变：当 m·ε≈1 以下，错误样本期望数不足，失配不可检测；大量论文报告的提升落在“验证地板”之下。
- 主动查询：若审计者可选择输入进行测试，minimax 速率提升到 Θ(√(ε/m))，且 Lipschitz 常数 L 消失，说明“输入选择权”能显著降低非参数难度。
- 组合爆炸：K 组件 pipeline 的验证成本呈 Ω(L^K·ε/δ^3) 增长，意味着长链路 agent/CoT/RAG 端到端验证会指数变难，必须分解验证或改变评测结构。2a:T72a,The work is an information-theoretic/minimax analysis of calibration-error estimation.
- Formalization: the calibration gap is Δ(p)=η(p)−p with η(p)=E[correct | p(X)=p]. The unknown calibration function Δ is assumed to lie in an L-Lipschitz function class F(L). The target is the minimax risk R*(m,ε,L)=inf_est sup_{Δ∈F(L)} E|Ĥ−H| for estimating ECE-like functionals.
- Main passive-evaluation rate: it proves a matching lower and upper bound of order Θ((L·ε/m)^{1/3}) (up to logs). The novel part relative to prior work is the explicit ε-dependence, which induces a phase transition and a “verification horizon”.
- Lower bound technique: construct two hypotheses/priors P0 (calibrated) and P1 (miscalibrated by δ around p0=1−ε) such that the ECE differs but the KL divergence remains small (scaling like m·δ^2/ε in a key construction). Apply Bretagnolle–Huber / two-prior methods (Lepski-style) to convert indistinguishability into a minimax lower bound. The paper emphasizes doing this directly in the Bernoulli observation model (with an alternative Brown–Low equivalence route in the appendix).
- Achievability: a histogram/binning estimator with an optimal bin count B*≈(L^2 m/ε)^{1/3} attains the same rate, completing the minimax characterization.
- Four “surprises” derived from the theory:
  1) Label-free self-evaluation provides zero information about calibration in the worst case (constant lower bound), unless white-box access identifies a low-dimensional parametric family.
  2) A sharp detectability phase transition around m·ε≈1.
  3) Active querying improves the minimax rate to Θ(√(ε/m)) and removes dependence on L.
  4) Verification cost for K-component compositions scales exponentially, Ω(L^K·ε/δ^3), making long pipelines/agent loops hard to audit end-to-end.2b:T436,Method: Multidimensional 2PL IRT (MIRT 2PL) + per-dataset anchor sets + Fixed Parameter Calibration (FPC).
- Each item i has a discrimination vector a_i over latent dimensions and an intercept/difficulty-related term d_i; each model has an ability vector θ. Correctness probability is sigmoid(a_i·θ + d_i).
- Concurrent calibration is unsuitable for evolving suites: it requires re-estimating all item and model parameters whenever new items are added, increasing cost and shifting the scale so historical θ’s are no longer comparable.
- FPC: keep previously calibrated anchor-item parameters fixed; when new datasets/items arrive, estimate only the new item parameters using a set of reference models that answer both old anchors and new items, thereby linking the new dataset onto the existing scale.
Use cases:
1) New model: evaluate only anchor questions, infer performance on the larger historical pool.
2) New dataset: calibrate new items via reference models, then predict old models’ performance on the new dataset from their existing θ without re-running them.2c:T4f3,The approach operationalizes multilingual capability as semantic fidelity under cross-lingual generation:
1) Round-trip evaluation: given a source passage x, the model translates it into a target language (or a sequence of languages) and then back to the source, producing x'. Semantic gaps between x and x' indicate failures in multilingual generation.
2) Scalability vs classical MT eval: no human reference translations are needed, enabling large-scale sample creation; judging can be done in the source language (the paper emphasizes English-side judging), avoiding low-resource evaluation bottlenecks.
3) Benchmark: LiT (Lost in Translation), 1600 samples across 8 language sequences spanning high/medium/low-resource settings, covering technical, pragmatic, and informal registers.
4) Scoring/diagnostics: uses MQM-style automated judging to quantify quality and categorize error modes (hallucination, omission, semantic drift).
5) Validation logic: (i) show multilingual math/MCQ benchmarks correlate strongly with math skill or factual recall (ρ≈0.94 / 0.83), (ii) show weak/negative correlation with multilingual generation preference, and (iii) show LiT round-trip correlates strongly with LMArena and reveals failure modes missed by MCQ/reasoning tests.2d:T44b,Key results reported in the paper include:
- Correlation findings: multilingual math reasoning benchmarks track math ability (ρ≈0.94), multilingual knowledge MCQ tracks factual recall (ρ≈0.83), but these benchmarks correlate poorly with multilingual generation quality / human preference (examples include ρ=-0.09 and -0.26).
- Real-world alignment: LiT round-trip scores correlate almost perfectly with LMArena user ratings (ρ≈0.94).
- Resource gap: open-source frontier models score >88 MQM on high-resource language sequences but collapse to <50 MQM on low-resource sequences (with the paper noting MQM>80 is generally fit-for-purpose; <80 should trigger mandatory human review).
- Robustness: on challenging round-trip constructions, model rankings match overall performance, suggesting the benchmark is stable rather than being dominated by corner linguistic phenomena.
- Behavioral observation: when instructed to translate faithfully, models tend to preserve awkwardness/errors rather than self-correct, making semantic drift/omissions reliably observable via round-trip comparison.2e:T49f,IDEA introduces semantically meaningful binary factors F={F1…FN} and decomposes decision probability via marginalization over factor configurations: P(O|Q)=Σ_f P(O|f)P(f|Q). Instantiation highlights:
- Factor inference P(f|C): instead of eliciting precise numbers, the LLM infers factor values; crucially, they use correlated sampling to draw joint factor configurations from the LLM, preserving natural dependencies (contrasting factor-independence assumptions).
- Decision model P_θ(O|f): an interpretable parametric model over the low-dimensional factor space, with parameters directly tied to factor contributions.
- Verbal-to-numeric calibration via EM: verbal probability expressions (e.g., “likely”, “very unlikely”) are treated as ambiguous; IDEA jointly learns the phrase→number mapping and θ using EM, treating numeric probabilities as latent variables to break the circular dependency between needing numeric labels and needing a model to define them.
- Parameter editing with guarantees: experts can directly edit θ to enforce domain knowledge/constraints, with claimed mathematical guarantees on the effect (details depend on the formal results section).2f:T85b,VISTA 是在线 self-distillation 框架，核心是用一个“validation-informed 的边际覆盖(Marginal Coverage)”来挑选并加权历史检查点作为“expert anchors”，再用这些 anchors 的软标签去约束下一轮训练，从而把中期学到但后期易丢失的能力滚动传递到后续参数状态。

关键概念与机制：
1) Trajectory Deviation 的度量（用于分析而非直接优化）：在验证集上定义某 epoch e 的正确样本集合 C_e，以及最终 epoch E 的正确集合 C_E；结构残差 Structural Residual = C_e ∩ C_E，对应“当时学会且最终仍保留”的样本；DeviationGap(e) 则刻画“当时会、最后不会”的遗忘规模（图2用黄/蓝柱差展示）。
2) Marginal Coverage（训练时的选择信号）：若某历史 checkpoint 在验证集上能正确覆盖一些当前/后续 checkpoint 失败的样本，则认为它对这些区域提供了边际覆盖，从而是该区域的 expert anchor。论文用“按验证准确率排序 + 扫描”来构造覆盖子集 {C_s} 并计算每个 checkpoint 的边际贡献，进而得到权重。
3) 目标融合与自蒸馏：每个 epoch 结束后，收集历史 checkpoints 在训练样本上的预测 p_s(x)，按边际覆盖权重做 coverage-weighted ensemble，形成 blended soft targets；下一 epoch 用这些软目标进行蒸馏式训练（并通过调度器 β_t 控制蒸馏强度/与硬标签的混合）。
4) 轻量化变体：为解决“存储大量 checkpoints + 计算开销”的问题，提出 lightweight 版本，声称可将存储开销降低约 90% 且保持峰值性能（具体通过减少保留的 anchors 数量/压缩保存信息等；全文在3.3与复杂度分析中展开）。

与相关工作差异：
- 相比 Temporal Ensembling/Mean Teacher 类方法：VISTA 不是简单时间平均，而是用验证集上的“边际覆盖”去做有选择的、区域专家式的蒸馏信号。
- 相比离线 checkpoint ensemble / Knowledge Fusion：VISTA 目标是训练期在线完成知识融合，推理仍是单模型；同时通过轻量化减少存储与推理复杂度。30:T697,VISTA is an online self-distillation framework driven by a validation-informed notion of marginal coverage to select and weight past checkpoints as “expert anchors.”

Main components:
1) Analysis metric (not necessarily the training objective): define C_e as validation samples correctly classified at epoch e and C_E at the final epoch E. The Structural Residual is C_e ∩ C_E; the DeviationGap(e) measures how many samples were correct at e but not retained at E, exposing capability loss masked by rising overall validation accuracy.
2) Marginal Coverage scoring: a past checkpoint is an expert anchor if it correctly covers validation examples that later checkpoints miss. VISTA sorts checkpoints by validation accuracy and sweeps through them to compute coverage subsets and each checkpoint’s marginal contribution.
3) Coverage-weighted blended targets: using stored predictions p_s(x) from selected anchors, VISTA forms a weighted ensemble soft target for the next epoch. Training at epoch t+1 distills the current model toward this blended target, with a scheduler β_t controlling the strength/mix with hard labels.
4) Lightweight variant: to reduce the practical burden of storing many checkpoints and computing ensembles, a reduced-storage version is proposed, claimed to cut storage overhead by ~90% while preserving peak performance.

Positioning vs prior work:
- Unlike temporal ensembling/EMA teachers, VISTA is selective and region-aware via marginal coverage rather than uniform averaging.
- Unlike offline checkpoint ensembles/knowledge fusion, it is online and keeps single-model inference, aiming to avoid inference-time ensembling and large checkpoint storage.31:T597,The paper uses the Averaged Partial Jacobian Norm (APJN) as the main observable for gradient amplification across depth. Key steps:
1) Modeling assumptions to make the analysis tractable: single-head Transformer; at initialization, adopt a uniform-attention approximation A_{st}≈1/n so attention becomes uniform token mixing; assume permutation-symmetric token statistics to close moment recurrences.
2) Derive layerwise recurrences for activation second-order statistics and for APJN through alternating attention and ReLU-MLP sublayers, extending prior APJN analyses from ResNets to bidirectional-attention Transformers.
3) Asymptotic depth analysis: show that pre-LN Transformers yield power-law APJN growth with depth, whereas replacing LayerNorm by elementwise tanh-like nonlinearities leads to stretched-exponential APJN growth, matching the “subcritical” regime known in earlier signal-propagation theory.
4) Attention’s role: quantify how attention modifies the effective scale parameter and critical exponent governing the asymptotic APJN scaling.
5) Practical knob (α): interpret α in Derf/DyT as controlling gradient amplification; larger α increases APJN growth and thus hyperparameter sensitivity; smaller α reduces amplification and improves stability.
6) Discuss the impact of the final normalization layer on observed gradient magnitudes near the output, connecting to known pre-LN vs post-LN behaviors.32:T4bc,Key reported results on SCBench:
- Models: Claude Sonnet 4.5, Gemini 3 Pro Preview, GPT-5.2.
- Overall accuracy: Gemini and GPT-5.2 tie at 57.6%, both above Sonnet at 34.9%.
- Consistent difficulty gradient for all models: Axiomatic > Constructive > Planning.
- Tools uplift (overall): Sonnet +3.2 pp, Gemini +8.8 pp, GPT-5.2 +6.8 pp.
  - Constructive gains are consistent: +4.3 / +12.3 / +15.0 pp (Sonnet/Gemini/GPT-5.2).
  - Axiomatic slightly regresses with tools for Gemini (-6.7) and GPT-5.2 (-4.0), suggesting tool overhead can displace effective reasoning.
  - Planning shows the widest spread: Gemini +23.6 pp (notably Hyper-Snake +59.3), while Sonnet and GPT-5.2 decline.
- Notable tasks: Fluid Simulation scores 72.7% (Sonnet), 68.2% (Gemini), 100% (GPT-5.2); Terrain Levelling is 0% for all.
- Delaunay Triangulation sees large tool gains: +56.0 / +36.0 / +48.0 pp.
- Token-budget sweeps (axiomatic, no-tools): GPT-5.2 improves from 0.04 at B=1,024 to 0.76 at B=32,768 then slightly drops to 0.73 at B=65,536; Sonnet rises from 0.12 at B=1,025 to 0.55 at B=32,768 and plateaus at B=64,000. Realized tokens keep increasing while accuracy saturates, indicating capacity limits rather than budget limits.33:T4ca,The approach is built around defining and stress-testing the “premium gap.”
1) A target model M_target answers question q and yields a binary correctness label y.
2) Train a probe f to predict y from hidden states h(q; M_source) of a source model processing the same q. Compare self-probes (M_source = M_target) vs peer-probes (M_source is another model).
3) Conceptual decomposition: h encodes z_public (input-derived, externally accessible features like domain/entity types/difficulty cues) and z_private (model-specific internal states such as retrieval success or internal confidence). Privileged knowledge is the part of z_private predictive of y.
4) Key confounder: on random samples, models often agree on which questions are correct/incorrect; peer-probes can exploit the peer model’s own correctness patterns as a proxy for the target, collapsing the premium gap.
5) Remedy: evaluate on disagreement subsets—questions where models assign conflicting correctness labels—thereby removing shared difficulty patterns and isolating target-specific signals.
6) Layerwise localization: measure the premium gap across layers to infer where privileged signals emerge and how they accumulate through the forward pass.34:T4da,The study combines behavioral evaluation with mechanism-oriented diagnostics.
(1) Constraint suite + prompt set: 40 prompts across four categories (education/explanation, how-to/advice, analysis/comparison, technical/detailed). Constraints are purely lexical/formatting but still free-form text: punctuation bans (comma/colon/semicolon), pattern bans (no bullets/numbered lists/dashes), word bans (no “the” or no discourse markers like however/therefore/etc.), plus two compositional constraints.
(2) Two-pass recovery to separate capability from planning: the model first produces an unconstrained answer; then it rewrites that answer to satisfy the constraint. High recovery of length/content indicates the model can produce compliant comprehensive text, but fails to plan for it when the constraint is presented upfront.
(3) Representation probing + base-model controls: linear probes on mid-layer prompt representations predict eventual response length before generation, with high R² (0.51–0.93) in instruction-tuned models and negative R² across layers in base models. This supports a mechanism where instruction tuning creates a prompt-level internal signal that triggers a low-budget generation mode under lexical constraints.35:T660,Task design: CLUTRR generates k-hop family-relation stories with minimal linguistic confounds; difficulty is primarily hop length. The authors rewrite each example to end with “Therefore, PersonA is PersonB’s”, turning it into next-token prediction. They restrict answers to a single-token family-relation set F (excluding in-law relations that often tokenize into multiple tokens), so the computation of interest is confined to a single forward pass and a single output token.

Probing depth usage:
1) Logit lens on the final position T: project each layer’s hidden state h_{l,T} through the LM head to obtain p~_{l,T}. Track (a) probability mass on the allowed answer set p_l^fam as a sanity check; (b) unconstrained correctness (full-vocab argmax); (c) constrained correctness (argmax within F). These quantify how early in depth the model forms plausible/correct predictions and how this changes with hop count.
2) Residual-stream contribution: compute relative layer update norms ||Δ_l||_2 / ||h_{l-1}||_2 with Δ_l = h_l − h_{l-1}, aligning with prior “later layers contribute less” analyses.
3) Causal patching: apply causal interventions to measure at which layers task-relevant information from earlier tokens becomes integrated into the representation used for the final answer, and how the required integration depth scales with hop length.

Model coverage: multiple open-weight families spanning ~120M to 14B parameters (GPT-2, Pythia, Phi, Qwen2/2.5, LLaMA). Fine-tuning experiments on GPT-2 and Pythia compare more constrained regimes (aiming to preserve general LM ability) vs less constrained regimes.36:T497,Key findings are primarily qualitative and regime-dependent:
- Pretrained models: limited evidence of adaptive depth. Some larger models reach plausible predictions in fewer layers on easier (short-hop) instances. Across models, increasing hop length tends to require more layers for cross-token information integration (per causal patching).
- Fine-tuned models: clearer but training-regime dependent. Under constrained fine-tuning (preserving general LM behavior), models do not consistently reach plausible answers earlier on easy instances, but they begin integrating information earlier in the network (greater early-layer involvement). Under less constrained fine-tuning, adaptive depth is strongest: more layers are used for integration overall, and plausible predictions emerge earlier for easier tasks.
- Data protocol: main analyses use 2–10 hops with 100 test examples per hop; longer-hop analyses require increasing the generator’s max-children setting.
Note: the provided full-text excerpt does not include the final quantitative tables/plots (accuracies, layer thresholds, patching effect sizes), so exact numeric deltas cannot be reported without guessing.37:T501,The methodology is structured as measurement triangulation plus causal interventions. (1) Representation views: per-layer hidden states are assembled into token-level matrices (preserving sequence structure) and dataset-level mean-pooled matrices (capturing the global manifold). (2) Spectral/information metrics: a matrix-based Rényi entropy computed from the Gram matrix eigen-spectrum is used to quantify intrinsic dimensionality / information capacity shifts induced by SFT, complemented by effective-rank style measures. (3) Geometric similarity: CKA and cosine similarity track Base-vs-SFT representational drift layer by layer, highlighting gradual decline with a sharp drop near the top. (4) Optimization proxy: layerwise parameter-change intensity (illustrated via attention projection matrices per layer) is tracked and aligned with representational drift. (5) Causal tests: layer swapping (mixing Base and SFT layers) and selective LoRA placement validate which depth regions are functionally critical. Based on these findings, they propose Mid-Block Efficient Tuning: update only a chosen middle depth band rather than applying LoRA everywhere, positioning it as an analysis-driven proof-of-concept rather than a replacement for advanced PEFT variants (QLoRA/AdaLoRA).38:T40d,Controlled noise injection + multi-pronged analysis:
- Noise types: label noise, typo noise, grammatical noise applied to fine-tuning datasets across tasks (sentiment classification, QA, MT) and model families (GPT-2, Qwen2, Llama-2).
- Attention diagnostics:
  1) Layer-wise KL divergence between clean vs noisy attention distributions (averaged over samples/heads/positions) to quantify magnitude shifts.
  2) Top-k Spearman rank correlation of attention weights to measure whether the ordering of attended tokens changes (distinguishing value redistribution vs re-targeting).
- Representation/task-information analyses (Sections 3.2/3.3): compare hidden states between clean and noisy fine-tunes and estimate whether task-relevant information remains encoded (the excerpt does not include the full formalism, but the intent is layer-wise probing/representation comparison).
- Robust vs vulnerable stratification (Section 6): split evaluation samples to test whether representation changes are uniform or concentrated on failure cases.39:T506,The authors build an ICL-theoretic analysis around a tractable surrogate: linear transformers solving in-context linear regression, under in-context suffix adversarial attacks.

1) CAT formalization in theory: they introduce an explicit trainable embedding matrix and generate adversarial examples by perturbing the resulting input embeddings (rather than discrete tokens), mirroring PGD-style CAT.

2) Robust generalization bound: within this “ICL embedding adversarial training” framework, they prove an upper bound on robust generalization. The bound decreases as the embedding-space perturbation radius increases, offering a direct explanation for why embedding-space adversarial perturbations can translate into robustness against token-space jailbreak prompts.

3) Spectral mechanism: the bound depends on the embedding matrix singular values; overly large or overly small singular values worsen the bound. This yields a concrete design rule: keep the embedding spectrum well-conditioned (neither exploding nor collapsing).

4) Algorithmic instantiation (ER-CAT): they augment CAT with a regularizer based on the variance of the embedding matrix singular values, aiming to compress large singular values and lift small ones, thereby improving the theoretical robustness proxy.3a:T475,1) Setup: modular arithmetic ICL tasks where the model must infer a latent linear rule purely from in-context examples; the authors vary task diversity, context length, and context noise, and analyze both in-domain and OOD generalization.
2) Bayesian lens: treat parameters as random variables and track predictive distributions; focus on epistemic uncertainty as the quantity reflecting model/parameter uncertainty.
3) Approximate Bayesian inference for uncertainty tracking: compare (i) IVON (Improved Variational Online Newton), an online variational/approximate-second-order method maintaining a distribution over weights during training, and (ii) a Last-Layer Laplace approximation that fits a Gaussian posterior around the MAP solution for the final layer.
4) Theory: a simplified Bayesian linear model analysis argues that delayed generalization and delayed epistemic-uncertainty peaks/collapse stem from the same spectral mechanism—slow learning along certain eigendirections delays posterior contraction; once those directions are learned, the posterior rapidly concentrates, producing an epistemic collapse aligned with grokking.3b:T407,The experimental narrative centers on aligning uncertainty trajectories with generalization transitions.
- Phenomenology: across modular arithmetic ICL tasks, test/generalization accuracy shows a sharp grokking jump after prolonged training, while epistemic uncertainty exhibits a sharp collapse at roughly the same time.
- Method comparison: both IVON and last-layer Laplace capture the shared “collapse-at-grokking” pattern, but differ in how they reflect OOD generalization and calibration under distribution shifts.
- Controlled sweeps: changing task diversity, context length, and context noise systematically shifts the timing/magnitude of uncertainty peaks and the grokking point, supporting the claim that epistemic dynamics are informative about learning phases.
Note: the provided full-text excerpt does not include the full numeric tables/plots (model sizes, exact accuracies, step counts). To report exact numbers, I would need the PDF figures/tables (especially the main figure and experimental sections/appendix).3c:T4c3,Scale and setup: 16,991 SWE-agent trajectories; benchmarks SWE-bench Verified and SWE-bench Pro; backbones GPT-5 mini, DeepSeek-V3, DeepSeek-R1, Devstral-small; 8 plan settings including standard/no-plan/6 variants; repeated runs to assess nondeterminism.
Key findings reported in the paper: (i) agents often follow the standard plan but with substantial variance; some are strict, others override adaptively as difficulty increases; (ii) having the standard plan improves issue-resolution success, while removing it reduces success; (iii) removing a phase hurts performance even if that phase is frequently skipped under the standard plan, indicating the global plan shapes local decisions; (iv) a bad plan is worse than no plan; adding seemingly helpful phases can degrade performance when misaligned with the model’s internal strategy; (v) periodic reminders reduce violations and improve performance; (vi) on SWE-bench Pro, compliance drops by 13% on average (explicit number) and phase-flow shifts (e.g., earlier abandonment of reproduction tests, validation via existing regression tests), consistent with higher difficulty and lower contamination; (vii) nondeterminism exists but does not overturn conclusions.3d:T57d,The key construct is a Thought Ti, defined as a persistent cognitive unit abstracted from a specific query Q, the generated answer A, and retrieved context Ki: Ti = Abstract(Q, A, Ki). A valid thought must be (i) query-conditioned, (ii) abstractive (distills a coherent knowledge point), and (iii) validated via confidence (ci) and novelty (si) checks to reduce hallucination and redundancy.

Core mechanisms:
1) Provenance tracking with root source mapping \hat{O}(·): for a raw chunk K, \hat{O}(K)={K}; for a thought T generated from a retrieved set R (raw chunks and/or prior thoughts), \hat{O}(T)=⋃_{r∈R}\hat{O}(r). This ensures every high-level thought can be traced back to original evidence chunks.
2) Provenance-aware retrieval metrics: redefine precision/recall using \hat{O}(Ti) to measure how much of the required evidence set Ki is covered by the thought’s root sources, highlighting recall gains beyond the immediate top-K context.
3) End-to-end pipeline (Figure 2 / Algorithm 1): retrieve from both KB and thought memory → generate answer → generate thought + confidence for validation → merge by similarity (threshold ε) to avoid redundancy → update memory by keeping only meaningful, novel thoughts.

Contrast to hierarchical RAG: tree summaries are static and query-agnostic; Thought-Retriever builds a dynamic, query-driven memory that evolves with actual usage patterns.3e:T4c9,NaviRAG consists of:
1) Offline knowledge organization (F_org): transforms a document collection into a tree-structured hierarchical knowledge base with continuous semantic granularity. Nodes represent semantic units from global summaries down to raw text chunks, with traceability from higher-level summaries to underlying chunks.
2) Online navigational retrieval (F_nav): a coarse-to-fine, two-stage evidence acquisition process.
  - Locate: use vector retrieval to select relevant semantic regions/subtrees (the foraging scope).
  - Forage: within candidate subtrees, an LLM agent performs top-down multi-step navigation, deciding whether to stay at the current level (use summaries/intermediate nodes) or expand to finer-grained raw evidence based on “information scent” and query constraints.
The final context is a mixture of initially retrieved segments (C_vec), intermediate summaries (C_sum), and on-demand expanded raw text (C_raw), then passed to the generator.
Key distinction vs prior RAG: not fixed-granularity multi-hop retrieval, and not global KG-style reasoning; instead, it couples a hierarchical semantic space with an adaptive, stoppable navigation policy to mitigate the granularity/noise trade-off.3f:T61d,The core design is a file-based visual representation with UID proxies and on-demand retrieval, aiming to decouple heavy perception from lightweight planning:
1) Externalize visual assets: images encountered during web browsing/search are saved to an external file system rather than embedded in the prompt.
2) UID-based textual proxies: each visual asset is mapped to a unique textual identifier (UID). The running context retains UIDs (optionally augmented with lightweight semantics such as thumbnail-derived cues), enabling long-horizon bookkeeping at minimal token cost.
3) Tool interface redesign: the agent is equipped with tools that support selective loading of visual content; the paper highlights a dedicated fetch-image tool for active perception when fine-grained understanding is needed.
4) Progressive workflow: plan and accumulate evidence using the lightweight context; only when a reasoning step requires visual detail does the agent resolve a UID via fetch-image, interpret the image, and write back textual conclusions.
5) Training pipeline: a synthesis pipeline creates cross-modal multi-hop queries; combined with existing deep-search queries, a strong teacher generates trajectories that are filtered/distilled (12K trajectories) to fine-tune Qwen3-VL-Thinking-30A3B into a specialized agent.
Key distinction from prior context management: it is neither pure summarization nor heuristic discarding; it treats visual evidence as addressable external objects with explicit references in the prompt, preventing context explosion by construction.40:T43f,The paper models a MAS as S=(P,G) with G=(A,E) a directed acyclic graph over agents. Each agent i produces a reasoning output r_i conditioned on the query and predecessor outputs; a decision agent produces the final response. CIA has two stages:
1) Reasoning Output Induction: craft adversarial-yet-stealthy queries that cause the final response to reveal or paraphrase intermediate agents’ reasoning, effectively turning hidden r_i into observable textual traces.
2) Semantic Correlation Modeling: treat the induced traces as proxy observations per agent and infer edges by modeling semantic correlations. To reduce spurious correlations from shared task/topic/style, they introduce (a) global bias disentanglement to remove shared/global components in representations, and (b) LLM-guided weak supervision to emphasize topology-related dependencies when learning/deciding correlations.
Overall, CIA operationalizes the chain topology → dependency in intermediate reasoning → observable semantic correlation in the final output, and strengthens it via debiasing + weak
